League of Nations Executive Council Opens Today, Foreign Minister Wang Requests Sanctions Against Japan, and Asks for Attention to the Bombing of Innocent Civilians, British Aid China Committee Calls for Aid to China 22

(Chongqing) The League of Nations Executive Council will convene tomorrow. Foreign Minister Wang Chonghui issued a statement here today, again appealing to the League of Nations to urge member states to take the following actions: (1) Take collective action to stop Japan's aggression in China; (2) Stop supplying Japan with military raw materials; (3) Sever financial and trade relations with Japan; (4) Implement the resolutions previously passed by the League of Nations, and please pay attention to the resolution passed on September 9, 1938, condemning the bombing of non-combatants, stating that the Japanese side's continued bombing of undefended cities, causing the deaths and injuries of dozens of civilians, including women and children, is intended to intimidate the Chinese people, but this inhumane behavior only serves to strengthen the Chinese people's determination to resist until the triumph of justice over force. (Reuters telegram, 21st)

(Chongqing) The Chinese Society for the League of Nations has telegraphed the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, to be forwarded to the directors of the Standing Committee of the Executive Council, requesting that sanctions be implemented against Japan to uphold justice and maintain humanity. (Telegram, 21st)

(London) The 105th session of the League of Nations Executive Council is scheduled to open in Geneva on the 22nd of this month. The application submitted by China has been placed on the agenda. The British Aid China Campaign Committee has issued a statement requesting that the resolutions passed by the League of Nations General Assembly and the Executive Council, namely, that member states should individually aid China, be immediately implemented. The methods are no more than three: (1) Do not supply Japan with war materials, including aircraft, which should be prohibited from being exported to that country; (2) Boycott Japanese goods, so as to inflict a major blow on the country's economic base in a short period of time; (3) Provide financial and economic assistance to China, so as to build the southwestern provinces, develop the industrial cooperative movement, and relieve refugees in the war zone. The above measures should be adjusted by a committee established by the Executive Council in order to improve efficiency. Recently, some member governments of the League of Nations have stated that they are willing to uphold the collective security system. If the League of Nations Executive Council can effectively assist China, it will be a great contribution to the collective security system. In addition, the United States is also willing to actively participate in aiding China, as can be seen from President Roosevelt's recent words and actions. (Havas telegram, 20th)

Ambassador Johnson Passes Through Japan to China 23

(Yokohama) United States Ambassador to China Johnson boarded the President Coolidge today to continue his journey to China to resume his post. Accompanying Mr. Johnson was his wife and others. Yesterday, Mr. Johnson met with officials from the U.S. Embassy in Japan all day. (Associated Press telegram, 21st)

Although the War in China is Fierce, Efforts to Suppress Opium Continue, Japan Openly Encourages Opium in Occupied Areas, Chinese and American Representatives State at the League of Nations 24

(Geneva) The Advisory Committee on Opium of the League of Nations recently continued to meet today. The Chinese representative, Hu Shih-tse, Minister to Switzerland, presented a report on the country's government's efforts to ban drugs, stating that the consumption of various narcotics is extremely harmful to the war of resistance, and it is necessary to ban them. Therefore, various effective measures have been taken to stop the sale of opium and heroin, and to reduce the number of opium smokers, hoping that those under the age of 45 who smoke opium will completely quit by 1941. All these measures have been effective and can be formally confirmed by neutral parties. For example, the annual report of the Shanghai International Settlement and the report published by the French government in Vietnam in 1937 are clear evidence. On the contrary, the harm of various drugs in the occupied areas of China is painful to speak of. The Japanese side not only does not prohibit them, but openly encourages them. Taking Shanghai as an example, since the occupation, it has been very different from the past. This can be seen from the report submitted by the Public Concession there last year. There are three objectives by which the Japanese side systematically poisons the Chinese people: a certain Japanese agency can profit from it to allocate funds for aggression; Japanese and Korean ruffians who are not tolerated in Japan are ordered by the Japanese authorities to come to China to sell drugs for a living; and to weaken China's resistance and lure traitors. The American representative, Fuller, spoke next, stating that the Chinese government is still working hard to ban drugs despite the difficult circumstances, which is commendable. Regarding the sale of various narcotics in the occupied areas of China, the U.S. government is still constantly receiving various news, which is very disturbing. The Japanese authorities have not taken effective measures in these areas to cooperate in banning narcotics, but in the view of the U.S. government, the harm of drugs in the Far East can be greatly improved. There are three ways: (1) The Japanese government should strictly order the authorities stationed in the area to prohibit the import of opium into the occupied areas; (2) The quantity of opium shipped from Iran to the Far East seems to have increased rather than decreased recently. The government of that country should immediately take effective measures to prohibit its shipment to the Far East; (3) The Portuguese government should take effective measures to cooperate in preventing the sale of narcotics and not allow Macau Island to become a base for drug trafficking. (Havas telegram, 20th)

U.S. Holds Commercial Week, Hull Delivers Speech, Peace Policy Should Be Based on Understanding, Not on Surrender to Force 25

(Washington) The U.S. "Commercial Week" opened today. The opening speech written by President Roosevelt was read on his behalf by Secretary of State Hull. It stated, "Maintaining peaceful relations is the ideal of the vast majority of countries in the world. The main goal of American foreign policy is also here. What we hope for and where our goals lie is in peaceful trade, so that normal conditions can be restored." Secretary of State Hull then gave a speech, strongly arguing that the policy of concluding mutual reciprocal trade agreements is beneficial to everyone. "The peace we speak of is peace based on understanding, not peace based on surrendering to superior force. Any attempt to replace fair negotiations with the threat of strong armor and sharp weapons should be stopped. The agreements that countries should establish must ultimately limit armaments and reduce armaments." Once the atmosphere of mutual suspicion between countries is eliminated and satisfactory agreements are established, the true wealth and true enjoyment of all countries in the world will increase accordingly. This is the plan we are promoting, both to do our best and to adapt to our country's position in the world. (Havas telegram, 21st)

Japan's Attitude Towards Europe Still Unknown 26

(Washington) It is reported that the Japanese cabinet's five-minister meeting has decided to refuse to participate in the military alliance treaty of Germany and Italy. Regarding this, diplomatic circles here have not received formal news from Tokyo that is credible. However, it is said that Japan will not sign a military alliance with Germany and Italy. From the withdrawal of the Japanese Marine Corps from Gulangyu, it can be seen that the government is unwilling to have friction with the United Kingdom, France, and the United States, so as not to increase difficulties in China. In addition, regarding the issue of protecting American interests in China, if the Japanese government's diplomatic policy has been determined, it is hoped that it will submit a note to the United States to explain its attitude. (Havas telegram, 20th)

(Tokyo) The central members of the Japanese cabinet met yesterday to discuss the attitude that Japan should take towards the European situation. Prime Minister Hiranuma, Foreign Minister Arita, Army Minister Itagaki, Navy Minister Yonai, and Finance Minister Ishiwata Sotaro were all present. There are rumors that Japan has decided not to participate in the military treaties of Germany and Italy, but that in the event of war, Japan will adopt a benevolent neutral policy towards Germany and Italy. This is considered to be pure fantasy and not to be believed. Political figures believe that the Japanese government has not yet reached a consensus on the above issues. The military faction and the younger generation all advocate concluding a military alliance with Germany and Italy, but the diplomatic faction and party leaders do not think so. They believe that the best policy is to conclude a military alliance with the sole purpose of resisting the Soviet Union. Beyond this scope is not in Japan's interest. (Hai Tong telegram, 21st)

Japan's Public Debt Last Year Reached More Than 43 Billion Yuan 27

(Tokyo) According to an announcement by the Ministry of Finance, as of the end of 1938, the public bonds issued by the Japanese government totaled 16,222,728,000 yen. Those purchased by financial institutions accounted for 8,701,921,000 yen (53%), those held by government agencies accounted for 4,992,593,000 yen (27.7%), and those held by private temples and shrines accounted for 3,028,213,000 yen (18.7%). This total is 4,329,775,000 yen more than at the end of 1937. (Reuters telegram, 21st)

British Foreign Secretary Presents Compromise Plan to Soviet Ambassador Again, Negotiations Now Taking Place in Geneva, England, France, and the Soviet Union Can Sign a Military Alliance 28

(Geneva) British Foreign Secretary Lord Halifax and Soviet Ambassador to the United Kingdom Maisky arrived here by the same train from Paris. Foreign Secretary Halifax immediately held talks with Ambassador Maisky, informing him of the details of the meeting with French Prime Minister Daladier and Foreign Minister Bonnet in Paris yesterday. Ambassador Maisky also reported everything to his government by long-distance telephone afterwards. It is generally believed that the agreement between England, France, and the Soviet Union can be announced in a short period of time, but in any case, nothing will be truly decided before the 24th of this month, because any decision must be formally established after the British Cabinet approves it at a meeting on that day. (Havas telegram, 21st)

(London) Regarding the organization of an anti-aggression group, according to the diplomatic correspondent of The Sunday Times, after Foreign Secretary Lord Halifax held talks with French cabinet members in Paris yesterday afternoon, the plan for cooperation between England, France, and the Soviet Union has been negotiated. Its content stipulates that England, France, and the Soviet Union sign a military alliance treaty, but it will only take effect when one of the three signatory countries is attacked. "This plan has distinguished between 'direct' aggression and 'indirect' aggression. Direct aggression refers to an attack on one of England, France, or the Soviet Union. 'Indirect' aggression refers to an attack on any of the countries guaranteed by the three countries. The military alliance treaty to be signed by the three countries is specifically aimed at dealing with direct aggression. In other words, if one of the three signatory countries is directly attacked by another country, the other two countries must immediately send troops to assist. If only indirect aggression is encountered, in other words, if one of the three countries, England, France, and the Soviet Union, guarantees one country, is attacked, and asks the guaranteeing country to send troops to assist, then England, France, and the Soviet Union must provide assistance in an appropriate manner. In this way, on the one hand, the advantages of signing an alliance treaty between England, France, and the Soviet Union can be preserved, and on the other hand, all concerns of the countries concerned who are unwilling to cooperate too closely with the Soviet Union can be eliminated. It can be said to be a win-win situation." (Havas telegram, 21st)

(Moscow) The dismissal of Soviet Deputy Commissar for Foreign Affairs Potemkin from going to Geneva to meet with British and French diplomatic officials is not taken seriously in Moscow. Moscow has never announced this matter. According to popular opinion, Potemkin does not have the authority to make policies, and there is no difference between him and Ambassador Maisky to the United Kingdom, who represents the Soviet Union at the League of Nations. Soviet officials and the Soviet press did not say a word about the remarks made by British Prime Minister Chamberlain at the House of Commons on Friday regarding the Anglo-Soviet negotiations. This is probably an indication that the Soviet Supreme Authority has not yet prepared to provide a new counter-proposal. At the same time, well-informed sources believe that Maisky has been instructed to continue negotiations with the British Foreign Secretary in Geneva. The result may be a compromise between British and Soviet differences, which is unknown. (Reuters telegram, 21st)

British and French Foreign Ministers in Paris Agree on Policy Towards the Soviet Union 29

(Paris) After British Foreign Secretary Lord Halifax arrived here, he held a long-term talk with Prime Minister Daladier and Foreign Minister Bonnet at the Ministry of the Army in the afternoon. In addition to a few experts assisting, British Ambassador Phipps also participated until 7:50 p.m. The official did not issue a communique on what happened. Prime Minister Daladier then met with reporters, saying only that the talks were extremely harmonious. British and French cabinet members and experts then dined together at the Ministry of the Army. There were eight people at the table, and the meeting continued. Foreign Secretary Halifax then led Malkin, a legal expert from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Stronge, Director of Central European Affairs, and Baker, Director of Intelligence, on a train to Geneva to attend the League of Nations Executive Council meeting. Soviet Ambassador to the United Kingdom Maisky also traveled on the same train. (Havas telegram, 21st)

(Paris) British Foreign Secretary Halifax, French Prime Minister Daladier, and French Foreign Minister Bonnet discussed the entire international situation for two hours at a meeting at the Ministry of the Army last night, paying particular attention to efforts to recruit the Soviet Union into the anti-aggression front. It is reported that this decision has found that the British and French views are completely consistent. British and French diplomatic authorities will continue to talk in Geneva. Before the two sides gathered at the Ministry of the Army for talks, Soviet Ambassador to the United Kingdom Maisky had visited Daladier. After French Foreign Minister Bonnet arrived in Geneva, he will discuss with Maisky. The general impression here is that although the talks between the British and French authorities are very satisfactory, an Anglo-Soviet agreement may not be concretely established within a few days. A major understanding will only be reached after the Geneva Conference. However, all sectors of the Soviet Union here hope that an Anglo-Soviet agreement can be established soon (Reuters, 21st)

(Paris) The newspapers commented on the progress of negotiations between Britain and the Soviet Union. The Radical Socialist Party's newspaper, Enterprise, reported, "Last night, the British and French authorities believed that the principles of the Anglo-Soviet agreement were expected to be established in Geneva by the 23rd of this month, and the formal signing of the agreement will be next week. This is also believed in Berlin. The German political police received intelligence on the 19th that the French military authorities had strongly urged the Polish army representative that Poland should be within the scope of the Anglo-French-Soviet mutual assistance mechanism on the day it is established, and allow the Soviet Union to assist with all its forces. It is reported that the Polish side has agreed. In addition, German Foreign Minister Ribbentrop was reportedly ordered by the Führer Hitler to transfer the trend of the establishment of an agreement between Britain and the Soviet Union and between Poland and the Soviet Union to the Propaganda Department, so as to instill this view in the general public in Germany, so as to avoid panic when hearing the news temporarily. The Communist Party's L'Humanité reported, "Soviet cooperation is necessary for France. Regarding this, the French Foreign Minister should take the British-French consultations as a starting point and explain it to the British government in detail." The right-wing Le Petit Parisien reported, "The Soviet Union has a non-aggression pact with France, and also maintains relations with Turkey. Britain maintains relations with France and has also concluded an agreement with Turkey. This kind of direct and indirect chain relationship is mutually beneficial. Therefore, it is firmly believed that Britain and the Soviet Union will be able to find a way to clear away all the difficulties in the current negotiations at one fell swoop." (Havas telegram, 21st)

Analysis of the Current European Situation 32

(Paris) Diplomatic figures here recently stated that it will become clear within the next few days which way European countries will turn regarding the Rome-Berlin Axis and the London-Paris Axis. The key is of unusual importance. British Foreign Secretary Lord Halifax is scheduled to come here to hold talks with French government authorities. He will certainly strive to continue efforts to organize an anti-aggression bloc. At the same time, Germany and Italy are scheduled to sign a political and military treaty on the 22nd of this month. From now on, the egoistic principles of these countries in politics will further develop into close cooperation in all aspects, especially in military affairs. These countries are also stepping up the exchange of views with the Japanese government, hoping that Japan will express its attitude before the signing of the political and military treaty between Germany and Italy. The diplomatic circles here believe that Japan's agreement to strengthen the Anti-Comintern Pact is undoubtedly certain. However, it is uncertain whether it will go a step further and join the political and military treaty between Germany and Italy. Japanese figures here also said that the governments of Germany, Italy, and Japan still need to conduct lengthy negotiations, but it is highly doubtful whether Japan will willingly accept substantial restrictions to resist the United Kingdom and the United States. As for Spain, General Franco, the Commander-in-Chief of the Nationalist Army, also seems unwilling to sign a military alliance treaty with Germany and Italy. At the same time, the United Kingdom and France are sparing no effort in organizing an anti-aggression bloc. The main key lies in whether the Soviet Union will come out to cooperate. If the United Kingdom and the Soviet Union announce the establishment of an agreement, they can effectively restrain the ambitions of the Axis countries. It is reported that the British government will submit a new proposal with a broader scope in accordance with the wishes of the Soviet Union. In this way, it is not impossible for the United Kingdom and the Soviet Union to reach an agreement. In addition, certain countries that were previously wary of the Soviet Union have also changed their opinions one after another. Among them, the transformation of Poland is the most significant. In addition, there are still several countries that are hovering between authoritarian and democratic countries, and will not truly join the democratic front until the negotiations between the United Kingdom and the Soviet Union are successful. This is the same as the significant impact felt by the Balkan Peninsula countries after the United Kingdom and Turkey agreed on a mutual assistance agreement. (Havas, 20th)

At 11:00 p.m., a Danzig city police officer arrived at the scene and advised the border guards to withdraw from the checkpoint, saying that he could not be responsible for ensuring their safety. The border guards then withdrew to the town of Siemianowice to avoid the confrontation. National Socialist Party members immediately destroyed the checkpoint. Dire Conditions in Inner Mongolia Under Japanese Military Control Commerce and Finance Controlled by Japanese Military Pseudo-Mongol Government Dominated by Japanese Advisors Suiyuan Cities Frequently Attacked by Chinese Army 40

The North China Daily News of May 14 reported a communication from Zhangjiakou: In February, a group of foreign journalists, under the leadership of Japanese officials, traveled to Suiyuan Guihua. According to information collected from the newspapers, after these people returned from this trip, they enthusiastically described the pleasant situation in Inner Mongolia. Almost like a second paradise, it was said that the area was peaceful and vast, trade was flourishing, local industry was developed, and the people were extremely happy and satisfied. If the reporters know that the situation there is similar to that of Zhangjiakou here, the reporter is quite surprised by these optimistic news. Therefore, some time ago, he returned from a trip to other towns with curiosity, but what is the basis for this? According to the reporter's observation,

The situation in Inner Mongolia is not only not optimistic, but in fact worse than before the Japanese military invasion. The prosperous export trade on which Guihua's prosperity depended in the past has now completely stopped. The reason is that the caravan roads starting from Gansu and southwestern Xinjiang are completely blocked. The Chinese army front line is only a few miles west of Baotou, the terminus of the Pingsui Railway. In the past, long camel columns slowly traveled along this ancient caravan road, traveling only one and a half miles per hour, carrying leather, wool, and other products from the Far West, and making huge profits. Not to mention the highly profitable opium caravans, all of this has stopped. No caravans now arrive in Baotou or Guihua. Secondly, in the northern Mongolian plains,

Bandits are rampant as before, so Chinese merchants who used to go to Mongolian yurts to buy products no longer risk going to these areas. In fact, the areas where people live have been devastated. Many villages are deserted, and the people are poor and in pain. Much of the land that has already been cultivated is now turned into pasture. On the other hand, the Mongols themselves no longer take their goods to the railway towns for sale, fearing that they will be forced to sell them at low prices set by the government. The only remaining export trade must go through the Mengcang Company. The company is nominally composed of six Mongolian merchants, but in fact it is entirely under

Japanese control and has a complete and absolute monopoly on all export products. Outsiders may not purchase wool, leather, or any other ordinary export items without special permission. When they were in Guihua, several German merchants also arrived in the area. Although they had special permits from the Japanese, they managed to purchase only the smallest amount of needed items after experiencing numerous difficulties, and left with very dissatisfied expressions. In short, the authorities have made it clear that they do not want outsiders to participate, and they are trying everything to prevent outsiders from entering the country. To stay in Inner Mongolia for a slightly longer period, one must obtain a special permit issued by the Japanese military authorities, and now it is becoming increasingly difficult to obtain such a certificate. Not long after the establishment of the "Inner Mongolia Autonomous Government," the Mengcang new banknotes began to circulate. However, no one trusts them. Although foreign exchange is strictly restricted and all exports and imports are controlled, the discount for exchanging Mengcang currency for legal tender is very large. As a result, in the past year and a half, all prices have doubled. Although salaries are also higher than before, they have not been able to compensate for the increased cost of living. Local retail commerce is still as good as before, but in addition to stores selling daily necessities, most customers are Japanese soldiers and civilians. In the past, the more wealthy Mongolian men and women flocked to Guihua every year to buy things, crowding the streets, but this is no longer seen. The so-called "foreign goods stores" that they especially liked to patronize have now become "luxury goods" display centers with sluggish business. In the countryside around the area, a lot of opium is planted. It is said that fields planting opium account for one-tenth of the total. This is probably because the supply of opium, which was often transported by caravans, is now being cut off.

The political situation does not seem to be as pleasant as the commercial and financial situation. Mongols and Japanese do not trust each other very much. Although the Mongolian government is nominally autonomous, it is actually dominated by Japanese advisors, and recently even manipulated by Japanese military representatives. The Mongolian princes know that they are in a subordinate position and are very unhappy, but they cannot do anything about it. The thousands of Mongolian troops recruited to fight against the Chinese army and suppress bandits, the so-called "Inner Mongolia Army," are extremely evil. The discipline is nonexistent, let alone combat. The Japanese themselves do not trust them either. These Mongolian troops, whenever they are sent out to suppress bandits, often loot villages and commit the most terrible atrocities, so the people hate them to the bone, even more than the Japanese troops. Because of the uselessness of the Mongolian army,

The regular Chinese army frequently launches attacks on various cities in Suiyuan, directly approaching the city walls without any losses. Sometimes, when the Chinese army waits for the enemy to approach and the Mongolian army sees that the situation is serious, they flee elsewhere. Because both the Japanese and the Mongols are dissatisfied, the reporter was quite nervous when he was in Guihua. Rumors spread throughout the city, saying that the "Mongolian Government" would move elsewhere, that the titular head of the government, Prince De, had already been deposed, and that the "Autonomous Government" would be completely abolished and the area would be under the direct rule of the Japanese military. Whether these rumors will become reality remains to be seen, but some changes will inevitably occur soon. As far as the welfare of the common people of Inner Mongolia is concerned, the current regime has certainly not made any improvements to the areas under its rule. In fact, as mentioned in the first paragraph of this article, the situation there is worse than in early 1937.

In short, there are three reasons: (1) general financial mismanagement; (2) the 90% of the population who are Chinese are as deeply opposed to the Japanese occupation as ever; (3) the Japanese have failed to win the favor and cooperation of the Mongols.

Japanese Troops Invading Guangdong Commit Further Atrocities in Heshan and Gaoming, Reinforcements Continuously Arriving in Guangdong for All Fronts; Chinese Troops in Heshan Mount Highly Successful Counterattacks; Japanese Troops Harass Various Areas of Zhongshan 41

Hong Kong dispatch: Over the past week, the Japanese side has been increasing troop deployments to invade Guangdong, having transported them from Taiwan. A portion landed at Humen in Guangzhou and were distributed to the three defense lines of the East River, West River, and North River, as well as to replenish the forces lost in Jiangmen and Hui City. These replacement troops were mostly dispatched from Humen to Rongqi and Guizhou, which belong to Shunde. It is speculated that the Japanese aim is still focused on the southwestern areas of Guangdong Province, while taking a defensive posture on the Northeast River. The West River has strong Chinese military strength and the strategic importance of the Zhaoqing Gorge. Mines are laid along the river to prevent Japanese warships from easily crossing. On land, Chinese troops tightly control the Lubao line, forming a strategic partnership with the Chinese troops on the southern section of the Yuehan Railway in the North River, controlling the Chantan Highway and containing the northwestern suburbs of Guangzhou. Therefore, the Japanese have recently only held Jiangcun on the North River Railway, temporarily connecting with Japanese troops in Huaxian and Conghua. The main force of the Japanese army in the northeast is concentrated in Taipingchang in Conghua, coordinating with the Japanese troops in Zengcheng on the eastern route. Another force is gathered in Longkou Village and Longxiang City in Huaxian, echoing the Japanese troops in Jiangcun. In recent days, patrols from both sides have made contact. In the North River, they are contending between Xin Street and the river. In the West River, the two armies are fighting for the Fengsong area on the Chantan Road. On the East River front, both sides have gained and lost in Fuhexu. Artillery fire occasionally erupts near Zengcheng. Along the West River coast, the two armies are facing each other across the river without major advances. This is a general overview of the recent war situation in Guangdong Province.

Since the Japanese army is taking a defensive position on the northeast fronts, the reinforcements arriving from Taiwan over the past month have mostly been dispatched to Jiangmen and Xinhui, hoping to gather the remnants, invade Heshan and Gaoming, circumvent the southern bank of the West River, and raid Guibian. After being replenished, the Japanese troops in Xinhui suddenly advanced along the Xinhui-Heshan Highway from the 11th to the 12th of this month. They first sent seven or eight aircraft to bomb key points on the highway in the Niushan, Duruan, Pingling, and Jinggen areas. No less than 50 bombs were dropped, but the Chinese troops near Pingling had strong positions and natural defenses. After the Japanese planes bombed at will, the Japanese troops rushed to Jinggen. The Chinese troops suddenly intercepted them, causing the Japanese to panic and flee. However, they were still unwilling to give up and sent 2,000 infantry and 600 cavalry to attack the Chinese positions in Jinggen, suffering heavy casualties. Since the Japanese troops on the Xinhui-Heshan Road were unsuccessful, they changed their plan to harass the coast of Heshan by waterway, hoping to support the advance of the Japanese troops on the Xinhui-Heshan Road and flank Heshan, attempting to spy on Gaoming. On the 13th of this month, 2,000 to 3,000 Japanese troops gathered in Jiujiang, along with more than 30 motorboats and a shallow-water warship, patrolling the Jiujiang River Qingyi area. At around 6 a.m. on the 14th, several Japanese aircraft were sent to bomb the positions of the Chinese troops in Gulao and Shaping, which belong to Heshan, to cover the landing of the land forces by motorboat. Six to seven hundred Japanese troops attacked Panbaokang in Shaping. The Chinese troops initially retreated strategically but then launched a fierce counterattack after the Japanese troops landed. The Japanese troops failed to establish a foothold and suffered heavy casualties, forcing them to flee back on their original boats. The Chinese artillery took the opportunity to unleash firepower, firing along Gulao, Heqing, and Shaping. Two Japanese boats were sunk near Panbaokang, and another was sunk off the coast of Shaping, drowning 50 to 60 Japanese soldiers. The Japanese army abandoned dozens of corpses on the shore of Shaping, and the Chinese army seized many spoils of war. That evening, the Japanese troops retreated completely back to Jiujiang.

While the Japanese army attempted to attack Heshan and Gaoming again, they also increased their troops in Daliang and other places in Shunde, attempting to invade Zhongshan County. In recent days, more than 30 motorboats have been seen in Rongqi and Guizhou, which belong to Shunde, and Toushan, Yinggezui, and the river surface connected to Zhongshan. Jiuzhou Island on the Zhongshan sea has been occupied by the Japanese army as a supply station. Near Sanzao Island, seven Japanese shallow-water warships have been seen cruising back and forth. On the 12th, they sent marines to land at Hengmen Yongkoumen in Zhongshan, but they were repelled by the Chinese army. On the same day, Xiaohuangpu in the county was also harassed by the Japanese army, and all the local food and hardware were plundered. At night, they fled back to Zhou, which belongs to Shunde. On the 11th, it was also reported that a Japanese plainclothes team was discovered in Nanping Township, the fifth district of the county, but it was fortunately detected and suppressed by the authorities in advance. After the unrest in the above-mentioned areas, the entire county was filled with panic. The county government immediately issued an emergency order to destroy the western section of the highway from Shiqi to Macau. On the 13th, an order was issued again to evacuate the population. For a time, refugees crowded the Qiguan Station, and those going from Qianshan to Macau were endless. Wu Fei, a member of the provincial government, was ordered to arrive in Zhongshan to set up the Sixth Guerrilla Zone. Wu has already taken office as the commander of the Sixth Guerrilla Zone yesterday and convened a county-wide military and political meeting on the 13th to determine a major plan for resisting the war and defending oneself. He then personally went to inspect the defenses of various districts to ensure everything was safe. (May 11th)

Two Young Tennis Stars from the Philippines Perform Yesterday and Win All Matches; Sanchez Defeats Carson, Anbon Defeats Li Guofan 43

Philippine Davis Cup players Sanchez and Anbon traveled from the Philippines to the United States to participate in the Davis Cup. Yesterday afternoon, they passed through the Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club and were specially invited to give a performance match, totaling three singles and doubles matches, held at the hard court of the French Chamber of Commerce. Five to six hundred Chinese and Western spectators watched, and the Philippine players won all three singles and doubles matches. Although the two had no special or advanced skills, they are young and promising. In particular, Sanchez's victory over Carson was remarkable. The two took the original round boat, Pias, to Japan and then to the United States this morning. The performance results yesterday are as follows:

Young, Strong, and Skillful

The two are unremarkable in appearance. Anbon is especially thin and small like a child, and it was thought that he was no match for Li Guofan. However, his physical strength is excellent, and his shots are steady. Li's failure was due to his lack of physical strength and stability. In the first few games, they were able to exchange shots, but later Li was exhausted and completely panicked, repeatedly touching the net and flying wildly. Anbon exchanged shots at both corners and volleyed, and was still calm after the match. After three to three in the first set, Li declined sharply, and the situation suddenly changed. Li scored in the second game of the second set. In the match between Sanchez and Carson, Carson dominated the entire court and won 6-2 very easily, but Carson was already showing signs of fatigue in the first set, and his running was not agile. This was probably because the season had just begun. In terms of skill, Carson was better than Sanchez. His volleys and chops were not as good as Carson's, but he was ultimately defeated by the rising young man. Carson gave up in the first set. Sanchez became more and more courageous in the third set. His forehand exchanges were indeed excellent. Carson was already unable to hit the ball with strength, and was only barely able to cope. After Sanchez led 4-1, Carson barely chased to make 4-4. In the tenth game, Sanchez fell to the ground to save the ball, losing the decisive point. Carson chased again to 5-5, and then took the lead at 6-5, but ultimately could not resist Sanchez's fierce shots and lost three consecutive games. In the final doubles match, Carson was already uninterested in fighting. There were not many wonderful shots from Squia. The two Philippine youths were still full of energy. Sanchez's style is quite similar to Qiu Feihai. His forehand is very good, but his hand is weak and he has not developed his other strengths. Both of them are young and will be rising stars in the East in the future.

Education News

Overview of Secondary Education in China (3) 54

Rewarding Graduation Exams, Focusing on Mathematics, Physics, and Chemistry

In the 27th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education stipulated that the curriculum outline for national secondary schools was not only for the use of national secondary schools, but also applicable to all public and private secondary schools across the country. It ordered various educational departments to formulate implementation measures and instruct all secondary schools to refer to them for implementation. This outline included five items: spiritual training, academic training, physical training, productive labor training, special education, and wartime rear service training. It aimed to add special education to normal education to meet the needs. In August of the same year, it also ordered all secondary schools to increase the teaching hours for music and art courses in junior and senior high schools. These two courses were each two hours per week in junior high school and one hour per week in senior high school to stimulate the spirit of resistance and awaken national consciousness.

In March of this year, the National Education Association decided on various cases of the secondary school curriculum: (1) Junior high school English may be changed to an elective course, and Chinese language, history, geography, labor (mainly housework for girls), or simple vocational courses should be added. (2) History and geography courses should be combined, and local history should account for one-third.

Equipment

Since the promulgation of the formal curriculum standards for junior and senior high schools, the Ministry of Education hired experts to compile standards for science equipment in secondary schools. In the 23rd year of the Republic, it announced the equipment standards for physics and chemistry in junior and senior high schools. In July, it announced the equipment standards for junior high school botany and zoology and senior high school biology, detailing the minimum, maximum, and general standards for the equipment of instruments, medicines, and specimens, as well as the estimated prices of the equipment. In the 25th year of the Republic, it also announced the equipment standards for the industrial arts part of the labor course in junior high schools, detailing the tools and materials needed for gold, wood, bamboo, rattan, soil, and other crafts. In the 24th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education, the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board, and the Chinese Cultural Foundation Committee jointly allocated funds and entrusted the Institute of Physics of the Academia Sinica to manufacture 100 sets of domestically produced physics instruments for senior high schools, which were distributed to high schools in various regions at half the price of 300 yuan per set. In the 25th year of the Republic, it was entrusted to the Institute of Physics to continue manufacturing 80 sets of physics instruments for senior high schools, 2,000 sets of physics instruments for junior high schools, 180 sets of chemistry instruments for senior high schools, and 660 sets of chemistry instruments for junior high schools, totaling 200,000 yuan. It was not completed until the end of the 27th year of the Republic. Due to the inconvenience of transportation during the war, they could not be fully allocated to schools, and most of them were stored by the institute, which would be adjusted and distributed later. After that, the institute was still entrusted to continue manufacturing, but on the one hand, it planned to raise funds to set up a factory in a suitable location in the southwest to manufacture domestically produced instruments to enrich the science equipment of secondary schools across the country and increase the efficiency of education.

Graduation Exams

The regulations on the graduation exams for public and private primary and secondary schools in the 21st year of the Republic stipulated the subjects and methods, ordering that students from secondary schools who did not pass the entrance exam would not be allowed to register for universities. Various provinces and cities held entrance exams. In the 22nd year of the Republic, the primary school graduation exam was abolished, and the secondary school graduation exam regulations were promulgated, abolishing the school graduation exam to reduce the number of exams in the last semester. There were better revisions to the scoring, calculation of grades, and announcement of the names of passing students, and the secondary school graduation exam committee regulations were promulgated to strictly organize the committee. In the 24th year of the Republic, the regulations were revised and promulgated, and the number of entrance exam subjects was appropriately reduced. The method of calculating the grades of each subject of the graduation exam was determined, and the grades of each subject of the school were also included in the calculation, accounting for 40%, and the entrance exam grades accounted for 60%. In the 25th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education reissued a notice to change the entrance exam subjects and stipulated: (1) The ranking of each student should be arranged according to the total average of their graduation grades in each subject. The calculation method of this total average is the sum of the grades of each subject in the entrance exam and the grades of each subject outside the entrance exam, divided by the sum of the number of subjects in the entrance exam and the number of subjects outside the entrance exam. (2) Only the list of schools participating in the entrance exam needs to be published, and the school grades do not need to be calculated according to student grades. (3) The junior high school entrance exam in each province and city may be held in more places than before. (4) The conduct and physical education grades of the school must also be strictly assessed, and they must not be allowed to participate in the entrance exam simply because their academic grades are still passable. In the summer of the 27th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education, due to the spread of the war, found it difficult for various provinces to hold entrance exams, and stipulated the entrance exam method. All provinces that have become war zones are temporarily exempt from holding entrance exams. The provinces near the war zones will have members of the Education Department sent to the schools to supervise the exams, while the provinces in the rear will still hold entrance exams. In the 28th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Education, in accordance with the Scholarship Regulations for Chairman Lin's 70th Birthday, used cash to reward the students in each province who achieved excellent results in mathematics, physics, and chemistry in the graduation exams, one student in each subject, and the top two students with excellent average grades in order to encourage them.

Law

Opinion

The Connection Between Law and Economics 58

— Qiu Ying

In modern times, humanity relies on economic strength to build wealthy and powerful nations and prosperous markets. While this is partly due to natural trends, it also depends on the completeness of the law, which has led to this rapid progress. If a nation's economic structure lacks legal support, it is like a rudderless ship, unable to navigate and reach its destination. Conversely, if the law is divorced from economics, there is no need for its creation. They are mutually causative and resultant, and the two contain inseparable and complex functions.

European and American economies have long embarked on the path of capitalism. To this day, they have reached their peak. Therefore, European and American countries, purely to cooperate with this economic system, have created many property laws and property protection laws to seek trade security and asset development. To follow the trend, our country must catch up and strive for self-renewal. However, due to various factors, the economic aspect is limited to coastal trading ports and a few cities, which have a roughly a structure, but are also biased towards consumption. As for production, it is still in its infancy. Other towns and villages still maintain our country's inherent way of life, with no modern economy to speak of.

Understanding this, one must know that although our country's civil and commercial laws are modeled after Europe and the United States, our country's economy is far behind them. Therefore, when put into practice, it is inevitable that there will be ridicule of a "maidservant imitating her mistress," and there is also the risk of focusing on one thing and losing sight of the other. This is because our country is under the oppression of foreign economies, and its foundation is exceptionally weak. Although there are emerging industries, they are just entering the front door of capitalism and have not yet been fully integrated. If the content of the law is too capitalistic, the welfare of the working masses will inevitably be completely exploited and will become increasingly impoverished, which is a hidden worry for our country. For example, the "rent increase problem" worried about by Mr. Yu Zhongluo and Mr. Zong Meng's "malpractice of imbalance between emotion and law" are all related to the livelihood of Shanghai's people. Although the current situation in Shanghai is unique due to the increasing number of residents who have come to Shanghai to escape the war, it is still different from the usual situation. However, the housing problem of the poor, when faced with the oppression of landlords, cannot be legally resolved, which shows that the factors of mismatch between law and economics have been fully manifested. It should be known that in European and American countries, the high price of housing is due to the development of industry and commerce, the gathering of political population, and the rise in living standards. However, the residents of Shanghai come here to escape the war, not only are they short of funds, but they are also mostly unemployed and have no access to loans. Their daily life is more difficult than usual, and their eyes are all falling. And the rich in general only care about their own interests, and they all use capitalistic laws to attack the poor. Although it concerns morality, it is also justifiable. In terms of human feelings, who would be willing to generously give up their own interests to be such a foolish fool who reverses the benefits? The so-called special environment of Shanghai can be said to be all special. On the one hand, the poor commit suicide, and on the other hand, second-hand tenants still oppress third-hand tenants, and other aspects of unscrupulous merchants still hoard and raise rice prices. Gold is the root of all evil, and it has exhausted the cruelty of the world—. Now, Mr. Yu Zhongluo wants to use social opinion to condemn the rich for their unrighteousness. Although this can alleviate the deficiencies of the law, it still depends on their character, and only good people can endure the end of their words. Otherwise, they will act perversely and stubbornly, and it will be difficult to subtly change them. Now, to treat the symptoms in an emergency, it is better to appeal to the authorities. If they can quickly promulgate a relief law to protect the lives of the general poor, and on the other hand, they must also rely on wise judges to consider the general economy in each case. It would be a great blessing if the majority of the poor were not suffocated by the difficulties of life.

Furthermore, the general public should be able to organize themselves with a sense of the masses to promote the modernization of the law. In order to improve the economy with "nation-building," complete the legal structure of the entire people. In general, there should be no defects, and it should also be able to conform to the principles of human feelings and benefit the people's livelihood. It is not far away. However, is it evil or not? I hope the legislative authorities will pay attention to it.

Mediation of Cases Should Not Lose the Spirit of Summary Procedure 59

— Xu Zuoliang

After reading Mr. Qu Yue's article in last week's issue on how to make mediation effective, regarding the hope that the court will improve the mediation methods, it is both thorough and detailed. I think there is still something to add, that is, when mediation cases proceed to litigation, they should not lose the spirit of summary procedure. According to the Civil Procedure Law, there are provisions for summary procedure and non-summary procedure (i.e., local cases). For non-summary cases, the delivery of summons for the date of oral argument should be at least ten days, and the trial period (Article 251 of the Civil Procedure Law) for summary cases is shortened to five days, and the facts and reasons in the judgment can only be recorded in essence (Articles 427 and 432 of the Civil Procedure Law), which is sufficient to show the legislative intent. Summary cases strive for quick and easy conclusion of cases to benefit the litigants. As for the provisions on requesting the court to mediate before filing a lawsuit (Article 409 of the Civil Procedure Law), its purpose is also to be quick and easy, so the mediation establishment has the same effect as settlement in litigation (Article 421 of the Civil Procedure Law), and it is not considered more solemn than local cases. Local cases do not need to go through mediation, while summary cases must go through this mandatory mediation. Moreover, according to Article 409, Paragraph 1, Item 5 of the Civil Procedure Law, if the nature of the legal relationship and the circumstances of the parties concerned can be considered that there is no hope of mediation, a lawsuit may be filed directly without mediation. Also, according to Article 419 of the Civil Procedure Law, if both parties in the mediation are present and the mediation fails, the argument for litigation may be made at the request of one party, especially for mediation cases. Although the court must mediate, under special circumstances, it is still possible not to apply for mediation, and if both parties are present and the mediation fails, the argument for litigation may be made immediately, which is more significant that the spirit of quick conclusion of summary procedure is not lost. Now, the Shanghai Second Special District Local Court, for summary cases, does not ask whether the parties have declared that there is no hope of mediation due to special circumstances, and directly files a lawsuit, and the court forcibly mediates all cases. The applicant who is present will be ordered to pay an additional mediation application fee of one yuan and five cents. (Applicants who are not present can be spared) If the mediation fails, the court will re-file the case and set a date for trial. By the time of judgment and execution, calculating the period, it takes two weeks from the filing of the lawsuit to the trial mediation. From the failure of the mediation to the filing of the case for trial, it often takes a month. From the delivery of the judgment to the final execution, it takes two months. Generally, for a summary case, from the filing of the lawsuit to the execution, it often takes more than three or four months (referring to those who have been confirmed in the first instance), which is more complicated than the conclusion of a local case. According to the reason, the court of the first special court applies the mandatory provisions of Article 409 of the Civil Procedure Law to the mediation of summary cases. However, the court of the first special court does not apply the provisions of Article 409, Paragraph 1, Item 5 and Article 419 of the Civil Procedure Law regarding the points that a lawsuit may be filed directly without mediation and that both parties present may make an argument for litigation. As a result, the complexity and speed of the case are actually opposite to the result of local cases, as if they have exchanged positions. Is this something that the original legislative intent could have predicted? Insiders said that the reason why the second special court must forcibly mediate all cases, regardless of whether the parties have applied for hope of mediation, is that the court's legal income is less, so it has to resort to this to seek relief. As for not allowing the two parties to argue for litigation, it is because the judges handling the mediation and the judges handling the litigation are divided into two groups, so another case must be filed. However, this is not without a way to correct it. If it is for mandatory mediation due to legal income, the court may order the receiving office to collect an additional mediation application fee of one yuan and five cents at the time of filing the lawsuit for those who file a lawsuit directly without mediation, and allocate the mediation and litigation trial together. The same judge will handle them separately at the same time. As for when the two parties are present, if one party applies for an argument for litigation, the judge handling the case may directly handle the litigation trial. If it is considered that there is a time relationship for the trial, it may be possible to increase the number of court clerks and reduce the number of cases to provide relief. If so, in summary cases, the spirit of summary procedure will not be lost, and the provisions of Article 409, Paragraph 1, Item 5 and Article 419 of the Civil Procedure Law will not be deliberately omitted and not applied again. This is what I hope that the authorities will improve and correct.

Summary of Judgments

(Shanghai Special District Branch of the Supreme Court)

When the court's verification of handwriting is sufficient for a judgment, it shall base its judgment on its own discretion, and it shall not be deemed inappropriate even if the appraisal procedure is not implemented. (Hu Shangzi No. 108 of the 27th Year of the Republic of China)

1. If the appeal petition does not state the reasons for the appeal, the appellant shall submit a statement of reasons to the original first-instance court within fifteen days after filing the appeal. If the appellant fails to submit the statement of reasons, the court need not order the appellant to correct it. 2. If the appellant has a lawyer as a litigation agent, or it can be recognized from the records on the petition that the appellant clearly knows that the requirements for the appeal are lacking, the court shall not follow the procedures of Article 439, Paragraph 2 and Article 441, Paragraph 1 of the Civil Procedure Law. (Hu Shangzi No. 109 of the 27th Year of the Republic of China)

A party who discovers evidence that has not been considered or who can use the evidence may file a complaint against the final judgment if the consideration of the evidence may result in a more favorable judgment. However, the so-called evidence refers to evidence that already existed before the conclusion of the oral argument in the first-instance trial of the previous proceeding. (Hu Shangzi No. 115 of the 27th Year of the Republic of China)

Legal News

Execution Does Not Extend to the Property of the Legal Representative 60

The Shandong High Court submitted a request for interpretation regarding the litigation costs of Teng County. The Judicial Yuan issued Instruction No. 1842 (February 3, 28th Year of the Republic of China), stating: "For the judgment of loss of a lawsuit brought by parents for their minor children to terminate a marriage engagement with others, the execution of the litigation costs may be carried out against the parents only if the parents are the parties to the lawsuit listed in the judgment. If they are only listed as legal representatives, the execution shall not be carried out against the property of the legal representatives regardless of whether their children have private property."

Method of Calculating Appeal Benefits 61

The Jiangsu High Court submitted a request for interpretation regarding the method of calculating appeal benefits for disputes over easement rights. The Judicial Yuan issued Instruction No. 1830 (December 31, 27th Year of the Republic of China), stating: "When filing an appeal due to an easement right lawsuit, regardless of whether the appellant is the easement right holder or the owner of the serving land, and regardless of the claims of the opposing party, the calculation of the appeal benefits shall be based on the amount of the increase in the value of the dominant land due to the assertion of the easement right by one party or the amount of the reduction in the value of the serving land due to the denial of the easement right. Also, for a lawsuit in which the plaintiff requests the defendant to return the land and demolish the buildings on the land or cut down the trees, regardless of which party files the appeal, the standard for calculating the appeal benefits shall be based on the active or passive benefits obtained by winning the lawsuit according to the portion of the judgment that is requested to be changed."

Legal Questions

(Question) A has a daughter who, at the age of three, was adopted by C through the introduction of B. After A died, C and the daughter agreed not to interact with A's family. Can they be approached to negotiate? (Hansheng)

(Answer) Since A's daughter has been adopted by C, she no longer has kinship with A's family and cannot be forced to interact with them. (Feng Meixue)

(Question) The divorce document states that the child is to be raised by the woman, and it is noted that education and other expenses are included in the alimony. Is the man's responsibility over? What can I do if I don't want this child? (Lu Renjie)

(Answer) Since there is an agreement between the parties, it should be handled in accordance with the agreement. However, there is a blood relationship between father and son, which cannot be severed by law. If one party cannot maintain a livelihood and has no ability to earn a living, the other party shall still be responsible for support. (Feng Meixue)

(Question) A certain lady lost her parents early and was betrothed by her relatives, but without the lady's permission. Is it legally valid? (Luo Xin)

(Answer) It is legally invalid. However, this is not the case if the lady ratifies it. (Feng Meixue)

(Question) A borrowed 5,000 yuan from B in the 25th year of the Republic of China, using land and houses in the concession as collateral, and there was a written pledge stating "the term is two years, if it is not repaid upon expiration, let someone (i.e., B) sell it by auction, without going through court procedures." Now that A has not repaid it upon expiration, can B sell it by auction after publishing it in the newspaper? Is this kind of special agreement valid? (Ding Yu)

(Answer) It is not legal to publish and sell it by auction on your own. You can only apply to the court for auction. (Yi)

(Question) A is from Jiangsu. More than ten years ago, because of disagreement with his wife, he came to Shanghai in anger and said that he would never return to Jiangsu, but the relationship between father and son has not broken down. After the August 13th Incident, A lost his job and his life became increasingly difficult. He borrowed 100 yuan from B, which has not been repaid. Recently, he wanted to return to Jiangsu, but his wife firmly refused. Although his son interceded, it was also ineffective. Recently, A was reported missing, then (1) Can the debt owed to B be demanded from his son? (2) Because of kinship, no interest is calculated, and there is no written note or witness. Can his son refuse to acknowledge it? (3) If his son denies it, what is the appropriate way to deal with it? (Cao Weiqing)

(Answer) Although A was reported missing, before he is declared dead in accordance with the law and his son inherits, the son is not responsible for repaying his father's debt. As for the loan without a written note or witness, it is not invalid, but when there is a dispute over the truth of the facts, the creditor should prove the truth of his claim, otherwise it is difficult to recognize that his claim exists. (Tong)

Answer to Mr. Sun Jilong The questions in your letter are without standards, so it is impossible to answer them. It is better to read more publications about legal knowledge and discuss with those who are familiar with the law when things happen. (Editor)

Research and Criticism

Victims in Private Prosecution Procedures 63

— Yu Zhongluo

Article 337 of the old Code of Criminal Procedure stipulates that the victim may file a private prosecution directly with the court with jurisdiction, and Article 311 of the new Code of Criminal Procedure, which states that the victim may file a private prosecution, both show that the subject of the right of private prosecution is the victim of the crime. However, the old law did not set a restriction that the victim must have the capacity to act, while the new law is attached with a proviso. Therefore, according to the result of comparative interpretation, if the victim of the old law is a person without the capacity to act, or a person with limited capacity to act, the exercise of the right of private prosecution may be carried out by his legal representative. (That is, the legal representative acts as the plaintiff in the name of the victim, and the legal representative conducts the litigation act.) If the victim of the new law does not have the capacity to act, he is not recognized as the subject of the right of private prosecution, and therefore there is no legal representative who can file a private prosecution on his behalf. Also, according to the illustration of Article 338 of the Bu Law, in addition to the victim, the following persons may be the plaintiff in a private prosecution:

1. Legal representatives, guardians, and spouses of the victim.

2. Relatives of the victim. Those who have the status of (1) file a private prosecution in their own name and are not bound by the wishes of the victim, which is called an independent private prosecution. Those who have the status of (2) may file a private prosecution only after the victim has died, but may not violate the express wishes of the victim. Exploring the legislative intent, it is appropriate to allow those who have the status of (1) to independently file a prosecution in the original public prosecution (Article 214, Paragraph 1 of the old law), and it is also appropriate to allow them to independently file a private prosecution in the private prosecution. Those who have the status of (2) are allowed to file a prosecution after the victim has died, without violating the express wishes of the victim, which is also a provision that corresponds to Article 214, Paragraph 2 of the old law. All of them seek to protect the interests of the victim in a thorough manner. The new law is said to expand the scope of private prosecution, but it strictly restricts the subject of the right of private prosecution, which must be exercised by the victim who has the capacity to act. It not only does not allow the legal representative to file a private prosecution on his behalf, but also deletes the provisions of the old law on independent private prosecution and the private prosecution filed by relatives after the victim's death without violating his express wishes. Therefore, even if it is a crime that is prosecuted upon complaint, if the victim does not have the capacity to act in civil law, his legal representative cannot file a private prosecution, and he must file a complaint in accordance with the public prosecution procedure before he can be investigated and prosecuted by the prosecutor. The scope of private prosecution has been relaxed, but the opportunity for victims to use the private prosecution procedure for protection is narrower than in the old law. Isn't it a contradiction for the legislator to say that restricting people other than the victim from filing a private prosecution is to prevent the abuse of fraud and extortion? Then why does the public prosecution procedure still set up independent prosecution and the provisions for allowing those who file a prosecution after the victim's death? The spirit of the legislator is not consistent, which is especially obvious.

What is described above is only the victim of a natural person. Furthermore, when it comes to legal persons, although Article 26 of the current Civil Law states that they have the capacity to enjoy rights and bear obligations within the restrictions of laws and regulations, it does not expressly state that they have the capacity to act. The Code of Criminal Procedure does not have the same provision as the Code of Civil Procedure that "those who can independently bear obligations for legal acts have the capacity to litigate," so it is not recognized that legal persons have the capacity to act. If they do not have the capacity to act, then when a legal person is a victim due to a crime, it should be restricted by the proviso of Article 311 of the new Code of Criminal Procedure, and they should not be allowed to file a private prosecution. Also, because the new law does not have the same provision as the old law for the legal representative to independently file a private prosecution, the representative of the legal person should also be interpreted as having no right to file a private prosecution. However, the so-called victim in Article 311 of the new Code of Criminal Procedure will be limited to natural persons. However, the interpretation of the Judicial Yuan is to expressly state that when a legal person is a victim, its representative may file a private prosecution, and it still maintains the meaning of "the plaintiff in a private prosecution is limited to a natural person or a legal person" when it was applied in the old Code of Criminal Procedure, or it also feels that the restriction of the new law is inappropriate, and it has to use this judicial interpretation to try to save it in application? The number and date of the new and old interpretations of this problem are attached below for reference.

Yuanzi No. 533 (August 7, 20th Year of the Republic of China)

Yuanzi No. 1394 (January 30, 25th Year of the Republic of China)
