As long as their energy hasn't waned and they meet the conditions for reproduction, of course, they can have children. I've seen Village Chief Xu a few times. Although he's over eighty years old, his body is still strong and healthy, clearly a long-lived man!" Zhu Aiqun said, "I know Village Chief Xu's family matters very well. Because his wife was delivered by me. People say: old people often return to their childhood, and Village Chief Xu is really like a child, completely listening to his wife's instructions." (116)

Reflections on "In the Dead of Winter" 121

— Qi Hua

“Let Us Live”

Produced by Columbia Pictures, Shown in Nanjing

After watching "In the Dead of Winter," I couldn't help but think of Paul Muni's "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang," and I also remembered an article published in a certain newspaper at the time of the film's release, "Law is Nothing More Than Human Sentiment." Yes, a person who has established many businesses for society and has a considerable position in society, who was a fugitive in the past, the law that protects human rights still impartially deprives him of his freedom. So "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang" is not so much an exposé of the darkness of the penitentiary, but rather the playwright's skepticism towards the law.

In "In the Dead of Winter," the taxi driver Brick is mistaken for a robber by the original owner, and because his lover Mary cannot provide evidence that he was indeed standing outside the church at the time of the robbery, he is sentenced to death under the "unanimous condemnation, no room for defense" law. The reason why the playwright created such a story is not like other films about wrongful convictions, with tortuous and bizarre plots, and finally discovering the real culprit at the last moment, to stimulate the audience; here, he also, like "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang," holds a skeptical attitude towards the law and some satire towards the disregard for human life by law enforcers. For example, after Detective Ewart discovered the bullet, he was convinced that Brick was wrongly accused and earnestly asked the prosecutor to postpone the execution, but the prosecutor's reply was "This is not my job." Also, when the detective and Mary went to New York to find out the real culprit and asked the police station for assistance, they were refused because the procedures were not met. Finally, Brick "gets his name cleared on a snowy night," and when the prosecutor declares to him upon his release, "This is my duty," Brick refuses his request to shake hands and thanks the detective instead, walking out proudly. These all clearly show the playwright's intent. Therefore, Let Us Live cannot be solved merely by a child (who discovered the robber's car) and the detective's efforts. Here, law enforcers should do their best to carefully examine the case, collect evidence, and give the defendant ample time to present counter-evidence, so as to reduce the occurrence of wrongful convictions (of course, it would be better if there were absolutely none); at the same time, the law is a dead thing, and how to weigh the pros and cons and incorporate "human sentiment" in special circumstances is something that legal scholars need to study.

The director's handling of this film is also quite lovely. He makes the emotions of each scene fully develop, and the editing is tight, and the photographer also contributes a lot. For example, in the two robberies, the photographer used strong and weak light to help create a tense atmosphere.

As for Henry Fonda, I agree with Mr. Li Zhihua's opinion that his portrayal of the taxi driver is very calm and powerful, and his passionate scenes with Maureen O'Sullivan are reminiscent of Charles Farrell in "Seventh Heaven." The performances of Maureen O'Sullivan (Mary) and Ralph Bellamy (Detective) are also not weak.

Economic Supplement

Analysis of the Recent Depreciation of the Japanese Yen in Shanghai 122

— Shi Yiwen

Since the "Huaxing Bank" opened on the 16th of this month, those who are unaware of the inside story have been uneasy, thinking that the value of the legal tender will suffer a major pressure, and the financial market in Shanghai will inevitably be affected. However, up to now, the facts have shown us that the value of the legal tender has not changed in the slightest, and the financial market in Shanghai has not shown any unstable phenomena, proving that the worries caused by the establishment of the "Huaxing Bank" are just the worries of ordinary people.

In fact, looking at the actual situation of the Shanghai financial market at present, it is not China's legal tender that is affected by the establishment of the "Huaxing Bank," but the Japanese yen itself. A few days before the opening of the "Huaxing Bank" (May 13), the black market exchange rate between the Japanese yen and the legal tender was 100 yen to 102 yuan of legal tender; but since the 16th (the opening day of the Huaxing Bank), the Japanese yen has fallen to the same price as the legal tender, and today (May 20), it has fallen to only 95 yuan of legal tender. (See today's newspaper) In this week, the Japanese yen has depreciated by more than eight yuan against the legal tender, and this downward trend may continue to develop in the future.

The depreciation of the Japanese yen did not start today. I remember that in June and July of last year, the market price of the Japanese yen in the open market was about 30% higher than that of the legal tender (i.e., 100 yen could be exchanged for about 130 yuan of legal tender). By September, it had dropped to 20% (i.e., 100 yen could be exchanged for 120 yuan of legal tender), and by January and February of this year, it had dropped to 10% (i.e., 100 yen could be exchanged for 110 yuan of legal tender). Recently, it has fallen below the parity with the legal tender. If converted using British exchange, in September of last year, the exchange rate of the Japanese yen had fallen from its benchmark exchange rate (one shilling and two pence) to ten pence, by January and February of this year, it had fallen to nine pence, and recently it has fallen to about seven pence. This continuous downward trend of the Japanese yen is certainly not an accidental phenomenon, but has its objective reasons. It is worthy of our research.

In September of last year, when the depreciation of the Japanese yen was at its most severe, I wrote an article for Wenhui Bao (see the economic special issue of the newspaper on September 20), pointing out the reasons for its depreciation. I am excerpting a section of it for reference:

"Since the outbreak of the war in 1937, no less than 200 million yen of Japanese banknotes have flowed into China. Among them, 150 million yen flowed into North China (mostly banknotes of the Bank of Korea), and 50 million yen flowed into the Jiangnan war zone (mostly banknotes of the Bank of Japan). The source of these banknotes is partly the funds used by the Japanese army to procure military supplies in the war zone, and mostly the salaries of Japanese soldiers fighting in China. In February and March (last year), as much as 50 million yen had flowed into Shanghai. By May and June, some speculators used legal tender in Shanghai to buy Japanese yen in North China, so Japanese yen from North China poured southwards, and Shanghai became a place where Japanese yen was rampant. The number of Japanese yen in Shanghai has increased. If it were possible to freely purchase foreign exchange, then its value would naturally not be a problem. However, under the strict management of the Japanese government, if one wants to purchase more than 100 yen of foreign exchange, one must apply for approval, and the conditions are very harsh. Not only that, but Japanese banks in Shanghai also refuse to accept transactions (such as documentary bills) that use Japanese yen to pay for the price of goods exported from Japan. (The purpose is to restrict the export of goods without foreign exchange) The environment in which the Japanese yen in Shanghai is located is like this, and the actual need for it in the Shanghai market is not great, so it has become a paralyzed currency, and its value is naturally unavoidable."

The above is the general reason for the depreciation of the Japanese yen in September of last year, but what is the situation of the current depreciation of the Japanese yen? First, let me introduce the Japanese side's own explanation.

The Japanese believe that the biggest reasons for the current depreciation of the Japanese yen in Shanghai are the following three points: First, it is the result of restrictions on the import of soybeans and soybean oil from Northeast and North China into Central China. In the past, the value of soybeans and soybean oil imported from Northeast and North China to Shanghai was about 2 to 3 million yuan per month. Currently, since Shanghai no longer imports such goods, Shanghai will have an excess of 2 to 3 million yen per month; the excess of yen funds in Shanghai will naturally cause the value of the Japanese yen to fall.

Second, the number of Japanese people coming to China has increased sharply, and Japanese yen has also been brought in large quantities. According to statistics for April, a total of 8,350 Japanese people came to Shanghai. If each person brings an average of 500 Japanese yen, then 4 million Japanese yen will flow into Shanghai in one month, and 50 million yen in one year. In the Shanghai financial market, which has no Japanese yen status, it is naturally very difficult to accommodate such a huge amount of funds. This will inevitably affect the exchange rate.

Third, Japan has restricted the export of goods to Central China, reducing the need for Japanese yen. Due to the reduction in the supply of Japanese goods in the occupied areas, the people in the occupied areas will naturally use the military tickets issued by Japan to transport them to Shanghai, exchange them for Japanese yen, and then exchange the Japanese yen for legal tender, so as to purchase the necessary materials from foreign or Chinese merchants with legal tender. Therefore, the result of the large demand for legal tender by the people in the occupied areas will naturally put pressure on the Japanese yen and cause it to depreciate. (See the Shanghai Daily News on May 19)

We also acknowledge that the above three situations are indeed the reasons for the current depreciation of the Japanese yen, but they are only superficial reasons, derived reasons. Fundamentally, it is the issue of Japan's national strength. In other words, it is the issue of the purchasing power of the Japanese yen. We know that since Japan launched the war against China, its military expenditures have reached as much as 10 billion yen. The consumption of military expenses is actually the consumption of material resources, which is also the consumption of national strength. If Japan's productivity is sufficient to adapt to the huge military consumption, then it would not be a problem for the Japanese government to mobilize the materials needed for the war through financial institutions. However, everyone knows that Japan's productivity is very fragile. Not only has it failed to supplement the materials needed for the war due to the massive consumption of the war, but also due to the massive consumption of material resources and manpower in the war, it has become increasingly unable to make ends meet in its productivity, and has entered a state of exhaustion. Now the Japanese government is only relying on the method of draining the pond to catch all the fish, issuing more banknotes and creating new purchasing power to requisition the savings of the people and maintain its external war. Looking at the amount of Japanese yen banknotes issued, it has increased from 15 billion yen in June 1937 to about 25 billion yen at present. (It once increased to 29 billion yen at the end of last year) In the twenty months after the war, the amount of new purchasing power (banknotes) has increased by almost one time compared with before the war, while its domestic materials (including savings and productivity) have not increased with the quantity of the forged purchasing power (in fact, it is decreasing). Therefore, the relative balance between purchasing power and materials has been lost. What is expressed domestically is the soaring of prices, and what is expressed abroad is the depreciation of the Japanese yen exchange rate.

The current depreciation of the Japanese yen in Shanghai is also evidence of the reduction in its purchasing power. However, the depreciation of the Japanese yen in Shanghai is not only against the legal tender (because the value of the legal tender has not changed), but also against all foreign currencies. However, in addition to the above-mentioned reasons for the reduction in purchasing power, there are two other reasons for the depreciation of the Japanese yen in Shanghai that cannot be ignored:

First: The recent depreciation of the puppet United Reserve Bank of North China has caused the Japanese yen to depreciate as well. The depreciation of the puppet United Reserve Bank is due to the fact that the puppet government of North China and the Japanese army need it in finance, so they issue it indiscriminately. Also, half of it is due to the people's fear of the value of the puppet United Reserve Bank, so they exchange it for goods (or legal tender). Because of the parity relationship between the puppet United Reserve Bank and the Japanese yen, the value of the Japanese yen is also lowered. Therefore, some speculators (including Japanese) use legal tender to buy Japanese yen in North China, and then transport the Japanese yen to Shanghai to buy legal tender, which makes the Japanese yen in Shanghai even more needed for the legal tender, and pressures its value to fall.

Second: The plan to issue banknotes by the "Huaxing Bank" will inevitably reduce the actual need for Japanese yen; at the same time, because the banknotes of the "Huaxing Bank" have no real reserves, they will inevitably depreciate due to indiscriminate issuance in the future (just like the situation of the puppet United Reserve Bank of North China). Japan knew this consequence early on, so it declared that the "Huaxing Bank notes" would not be linked to the Japanese yen, which is tantamount to reflecting the emptiness of the Japanese yen's foundation. Therefore, most people (including Japanese) dare not collect Japanese yen, but would rather exchange it for legal tender with a stable value (or buy goods), which makes the value of the legal tender relatively higher, and makes the value of the Japanese yen fall step by step.

The above two reasons are so powerful in promoting the depreciation of the Japanese yen in Shanghai precisely because the purchasing power of the Japanese yen has been fundamentally reduced. It can also be said to be the result of inflation. Therefore, what is expressed by this is not only the shaking of the external credit of the Japanese yen, but also the significant losses suffered by Japan in the war against China. If the war against China cannot be ended, then the consumption of Japan's national strength will definitely increase day by day, and the purchasing power of the Japanese yen will also deteriorate day by day. The result of the deterioration of the purchasing power of the Japanese yen will not only make it difficult to maintain the war, but also promote the total collapse of its entire national economy. The current continuous depreciation of the Japanese yen shows that Japan is already on the road to total collapse. On the contrary: the current stability of the value of the legal tender and the relative increase in value against the Japanese yen are proof of the correctness of China's strategy of protracted attrition warfare, indicating that China has already moved towards a dominant position in the military, and the final victory is not a problem.

"Huaxing Bank" and the Shanghai Market 123

— Xinhai

The so-called "Huaxing Commercial Bank" has a negligible impact on the Shanghai market; although there are rumors in the market, as long as ordinary people do not disturb themselves, "Huaxing" cannot do anything about it.

However, when the news of the establishment of "Huaxing" came out, the forward exchange rate of the legal tender once tightened, which was probably due to the fact that the market was not calm at first and did not fully understand it; and when it recognized its nature and tricks, it immediately stabilized as usual. However, on the day of its opening on the 16th, various unfounded rumors were spread again from nowhere, causing the sensitive market to be foolishly manipulated once again; the black market price of public bonds suddenly dropped as a result. The rumors I heard are roughly in four categories:

1. It is said that in order to resist "Huaxing's" attempt to seize legal tender, the National Government plans to replace the legal tender of five yuan or more with banknotes bearing a chop, leaving only small denominations of currency below one yuan in circulation in the market. Only banknotes bearing a chop can be used to purchase foreign exchange in the future.

2. It is said that the National Government will henceforth make all principal and interest payments on public bonds in Chongqing, no longer using the method of "paying in Chongqing once and paying in Shanghai in six installments," in order to reduce the inflow of legal tender funds into Shanghai.

3. It is said that the legal tender of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications will be gradually withdrawn, allowing the banknotes and miscellaneous currencies issued by the remaining eight legal commercial banks to circulate, and these non-Central, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications banknotes will not be eligible to purchase foreign exchange.

4. It is said that the existing legal tender foreign exchange stabilization fund will be divided among China, Britain, and the United States, and will only be supplied to China, Britain, and the United States. Ordinary needs will not be supplied for the time being.

These rumors caused some people in the market to be impulsive, which is really too lacking in judgment. First of all, the wise authorities would never take this inferior strategy of undermining the credibility of the legal tender. Because, if only banknotes with a chop are allowed to purchase foreign exchange, then the legal tender to banknotes with a chop will inevitably be at a discount. The legal tender at a discount is no different from the depreciation of the legal tender; moreover, the legal tender can still purchase foreign exchange after paying the discount and obtaining banknotes with a chop. How can the attempt of the pseudo "Huaxing" to absorb legal tender and seize foreign exchange be prevented simply by adding a procedure of converting to banknotes with a chop? Presumably, this rumor originated from the discount of the banknotes with a chop of foreign merchant banks. Foreign merchant banks use banknotes with a chop to avoid the complexity of legal tender calculations, but this cannot be regarded as the circulation of banknotes with a chop.

The second point is equally ridiculous. Even if the National Government wants to shrink the legal tender in the war zone, it does not need to harp on this old tune. Moreover, the government has always been determined to maintain its debt credibility; it will not revoke its previous promise, and the government can certainly restrict the flow of legal tender to Shanghai from other aspects. Why must it plan on the payment of principal and interest on public bonds?

The third point is also impossible. If the government withdraws the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, and allows miscellaneous currencies to circulate, wouldn't it be tantamount to the government slapping itself in the face? The banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are legal tender, and those issued by other commercial banks are also legal tender. The former can purchase foreign exchange, while the latter cannot. Isn't this destroying the already unified currency system? Even in the Tianjin concession, there will never be a withdrawal of legal tender. On the contrary, when funds from North China fled south in droves, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications in Tianjin restricted Shanghai exchange in order to maintain the original circulation of legal tender in North China. Because if the legal tender is withdrawn, there will be no currency available for circulation in the concession, and then the pseudo-currency can take the opportunity to seize the circulation area of the legal tender. Would the government be so stupid?

Finally, everyone knows that the establishment of the legal tender stabilization fund is to stabilize the external value of the legal tender. Therefore, anyone who holds legal tender, whether they are Chinese merchants, British merchants, etc., can purchase foreign exchange if necessary. The holders of legal tender do have nationalities, but the value of legal tender is definitely not different due to the different nationalities of the holders. Therefore, it is not worth a knowledgeable person's smile to say that the legal tender stabilization fund will be divided among the three countries. There are many ways to prevent the inflow into the pseudo "Huaxing"! For example, not allowing inland products to fall into the hands of the Japanese puppets and not buying Japanese goods are all ways.

In fact, even without the above analysis, the stability of the market today and the recovery of various bonds can prove the incredibility of these rumors.

China's Cotton Industry Since the Start of the War (Translated from the "Millard's Review") 124

— Boming

The published figures for the losses and damages suffered by Chinese textile mills, especially yarn mills, during the Sino-Japanese War are truly alarming. The work stoppages and destruction of factory equipment have an even greater impact on the welfare and prosperity of capitalists and workers, because the textile industry in China is an important industry that employs more labor and invests more capital than any other industry. The information we have obtained from various organizations, textile mill managers, foreign agencies, and custodians, or from various parties related to these textile mills, can be reliably trusted.

However, there are also some factory buildings that have been used by the Japanese army as military hospitals or general headquarters. Except for the Japanese, no one is allowed to enter. Therefore, the actual situation of these textile mills is almost impossible to know for sure. Only a rough estimate of the degree of damage to the buildings can be made. Regarding the machinery inside, it is difficult to know for sure. According to various sources, the Japanese army has transported the machinery and motors of Chinese yarn mills in the occupied areas of Shanghai to Qingdao and installed them in Japanese yarn mills.

The current situation of Chinese yarn mills can be divided into the following categories:

(1) Twenty-six mills have been forcibly taken over by the Japanese army and are now being operated by the Japanese army for their own benefit, with 681,960 spindles, 42,950 doubling spindles, and 6,244 looms.

The yarn mills in the three provinces of Lu, Jin, and Yu have all been taken over and are used to weave military uniforms or as military machine repair shops. These confiscated factories only employ Chinese coolies and ordinary workers. Some Chinese yarn mills managed and operated by foreigners have also been taken over. For example, the Dasheng Yarn Mills No. 1, 3, and 8, operated by the German company Arnhold & Co., were forcibly taken over on March 3 this year. Although the German embassy has been negotiating with the Japanese side, there has been no result so far. In short, the Chinese-owned yarn mills forcibly taken over by the Japanese side account for about one-quarter of the total number of spindles.

(2) Some or severely damaged, and now being repaired by the Japanese, 8,007 looms.

Most of these textile mills are in Jiangsu Province outside the Shanghai Concession area. Chinese textile mills in Wuxi and Changzhou are completely included in this category.

(3) Five textile mills have been occupied by the Japanese army as military hospitals and general headquarters, with 276,830 spindles, 44,266 doubling spindles, and 2,115 looms.

Most of these textile mills are around Shanghai. The No. 1, 2, and 3 mills of Wing On Textile Co., Ltd., have all been occupied, and people of any nationality are not allowed to enter.

(4) Fifteen textile mills are operating normally in the Shanghai Concession area and areas where no war has occurred, with 437,562 spindles, 34,898 doubling spindles, and 2,610 looms.

Most of these textile mills are in the center of the Shanghai International Settlement and in the two provinces of Shaanxi and Yunnan, and have made huge profits since the start of the war.

(5) Five textile mills (including one large dyeing and weaving mill) are operated by the Japanese side, ostensibly according to the so-called Sino-Japanese cooperation plan, i.e., the Japanese get 51% of the net profit and the Chinese get 49%, with 42,328 spindles, 7,980 doubling spindles, and 1,500 looms.

The managers of these textile mills have compromised with the Japanese side and have made some secret arrangements. Three of them are in Shanghai, one is in Wuhu, Anhui Province, and one is in Tangshan, Hebei Province.

(6) Eleven textile mills have moved some of their machinery to inland cities such as Chongqing and Xi'an and to the Shanghai International Settlement, with 315,162 spindles, 5,600 doubling spindles, and 2,293 looms.

Most of these relocated textile mills have changed their names, and many are registered under foreign names or are operated by the Bank of China.

(7) The machinery of the No. 1 Hubei Yarn Mill, now including 88,160 spindles and 648 looms, is stored in a foreign warehouse in Hankou. The mill is currently in the custody of the British company Tolly & Co.

(8) Eight textile mills are currently shut down in less favorable central locations within the Japanese-occupied area due to frequent attacks by Chinese mobile units or difficulties in transportation and communication, with 172,044 spindles, 8,400 variable spindles, and 920 looms.

The Hengda Yarn Mill in Pudong is said to be shut down due to the activity of Chinese mobile units, and other textile mills on the outskirts of Shanghai are also shut down for the same reason.

(9) Textile mills that were shut down during the war and have resumed operation since last year include: Chongxin in Zhabei, registered under British name, and Ewo Cotton Mill in Yangshupu district.

(10) The following textile mills are said to have had their machinery transported out by the Japanese side: Hengfeng Textile Company, Shenxin Yarn Mill No. 7, registered under a British name, Dahua Dyeing and Weaving Company, all of the above are in Yangshupu, and Zhentai Yarn Mill in Zhabei registered under British name.

(11) The following mills have been opened in Shanghai since the war: Anda Textile Company, 15,000 spindles, Zhongfang Company, 26,000 spindles and 300 looms, China Yarn Mill, 15,000 spindles (all of the above are registered under British names), Guomian Yarn Manufacturing Company, 26,000 spindles, Defang Textile Company, 10,340 spindles and 128 looms, (all of the above are registered under American names), Rongfeng Yarn Mill, 10,000 spindles, and Feng Textile Company, 5,000 spindles and 150 looms, Xinsheng Yarn Mill, 10,360 spindles, Zhaoxing Yarn Mill, 8,400 spindles, Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Mill, China Woolen Mill, 4,000 woolen spindles and 100 looms.

The machinery of the above mills did not come from inland cities such as Wuxi. (To be continued)

Supply and Demand of Yarn and Cloth Amidst Rising Prices (Continued) 125

— Wang Fuli

Reading Table 7, the number of Chinese textile machines has been reduced to such a large extent. Although the output of yarn and cloth does not necessarily decrease in the same proportion due to differences in thickness and types, it is easy to infer that the supply is not meeting the demand. Even when combined with what British and Japanese merchants own or occupy, as shown in Table 8.

Reading Table 8, it can be seen that the quantity of yarn and cloth that the country can supply, even if the people do not buy all domestic products, is reduced by about 40% compared to before the war. This one point alone already leaves a lot of room for price increases, let alone other various reasons. The reason why it has maintained a considerable high price until now is well-founded. To meet the needs of the times, there are still a considerable number of new machines ordered before the war and old machines moved from the war zone that are being actively set up in the rear and can be opened soon. In addition, Mu's hand spinning machines with machine properties, sophisticated hand spinning weaving, Guangshi hand spinning machines, and Indian spinning waterwheel spinning are being planned one after another. It is firmly believed that a considerable production time will be achieved in the near future. The market price of yarn and cloth, which is necessary for daily use, will also fall accordingly. Let's wait and see. (End)

Silk and Tea: Zhejiang Native Silkworm Cocoons Have Entered the Market; Cocoon Merchants Compete to Buy, Breaking the Price Limit; Shanghai and Wuxi Cocoon Collection is in Preparation 126

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Spring Cocoons: Have been launched one after another. Native cocoons in Zhejiang Province have exceeded the price limit. In the areas of Suzhou, Wuxi, etc., the local varieties have reached the stage of dormancy and leaf opening, and are about to be placed on the cocooning frames. The progress is quite good. Now, based on communications from various places, the main points are recorded as follows:

(1) Zhejiang Province

Zhejiang is located south of Jiangsu, and its climate is more temperate than Jiangsu. The sprouting of silkworms occurs earlier accordingly. Therefore, the spring cocoons are launched in the market about half a month earlier than in Jiangsu Province. This year, the native cocoons in various counties of Hangzhou Prefecture have all been launched in the market. The local varieties will be launched at the end of this month at the latest. The cocoon industry association has agreed to set a price limit of 45 yuan per dan for native fresh cocoons. The cocoon firms officially started collecting goods on the 18th. However, due to the unfavorable climate in Zhejiang Province this year, the humidity was uneven during the silkworm rearing period. As a result, the output has decreased. The cocoon firms have received very few goods in the past two days. The cocoon merchants, seeing that the silk market in Shanghai will not fall in the near future, fear that they will not receive enough goods. Therefore, each cocoon firm has released bids to solicit goods, and the market price has presented a chaotic situation. The total price of cocoons in the past two days has jumped from the limit price of 45 yuan to 52 yuan, an increase of 7 yuan. According to the opinion of people in the industry, the market price is still likely to continue to rise. It is expected that when the local cocoons are launched at the end of the month, the opening price will be as high as 80 yuan.

(2) Wuxi

The cocoons produced in this county are best known in the southwest region. In recent years, the north region has also been rising rapidly. The silkworms in the four townships have all entered the stage of dormancy and leaf opening. From the time of hatching to the time of dormancy, the spring breeze is blowing gently, and the climate is mild. Therefore, the development process is exceptionally good. The silkworms are healthy and there are no symptoms of disease. If there are no major disturbances from the time of dormancy to the time of cocooning, they can steadily move towards a healthy state. According to investigations, the cocoons are very good this year in Zhangjing Bridge, Yuqi, Luoshe in the north township, and Shitang, Nanqiao, Fangquan, Xushe in the south township, near Jiangyin, and Zhang Miaoshe, etc. Among them, several places have already started cocooning. Because of the early and late hatching, the launch in the market also has a sequence. In the areas of Suzhou and Wuxi, the scales can be opened in early June.

(3) Shanghai

The cocoon firms in the guerrilla zone leased by the silk manufacturers in Shanghai are busy preparing for the collection of cocoons and other necessary matters due to the imminent launch of new cocoons. The Shanghai financial community is also happy to provide assistance on the issue of silk cocoon deposits. As soon as the first batch of goods arrives in Shanghai, a loan can be obtained by pledging the warehouse receipt. The manufacturers then use the loan to purchase goods, and so on in an endless stream until the end of the cocoon season. This is not only of great benefit to the silk industry in Shanghai, but also indirectly benefits the prosperity of our country's export goods. Regarding the saying that all ports are prohibited from shipping goods, the factories in Shanghai are determined to do everything possible to deal with it, enduring the pressure. Recently, orderly plans have been made, and people have been sent out to mediate. Therefore, it is feared that the situation has eased slightly. (Xiang)

Old News from the Xin Xin Bao 67 Years Ago (35)

(See this newspaper from May of the 11th year of Tongzhi of the Qing Dynasty)

Western Envoys Granted Audience with the Emperor 135

The Emperor has allowed Western envoys to pay respects, exempting them from performing the three kneelings and nine prostrations ritual. That the Great Qing Emperor is able to allow non-observance of the central rituals is truly the epitome of friendly neighborliness. During the Qianlong era, an English envoy named Macartney led an embassy to court, bringing tribute. Upon entering, China presented him with the ritual of paying respects. Macartney declined due to unfamiliarity. The Emperor issued an edict exempting him from performing the prostration ritual, only following the ritual of monarchs of other European countries when paying respects. Once agreed, Emperor Qianlong met Macartney in the Hall of Supreme Harmony. Macartney held a golden box, adorned with pearls, containing the English Emperor's congratulatory message, raised it with both hands, ascended the steps, and presented it to the throne. Thereafter, Macartney paid respects several times in the capital and Rehe, all without prostrating.

Anglo-Chinese College 136

The Anglo-Chinese College has completed the rebuilding of its buildings on the southern side of the New Bridge, near the western side of the British Consulate. It has now engaged famous Western teachers and Chinese classical teachers to teach students, enabling them to understand both Chinese and foreign languages. All teaching methods are clear and straightforward. The head teacher is Englishman Ge. Classes are held from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM every morning. English teachers teach Western languages, writing, and mathematics. From 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM in the afternoon, Chinese teachers teach Chinese studies. The college's books, both Chinese and foreign, can be borrowed and do not need to be self-provided. Paper, ink, brushes, and inkstones are all provided. The tuition fee is 60 taels per year, payable in advance for one quarter, 15 taels of silver for three months. Those who wish to send their children to study should contact the Taifeng Foreign Firm on Sanma Road to make arrangements.

Record of Firelight Completed 137

Last month, in the urban and rural areas of Suzhou, a red light suddenly appeared in the sky at night, accompanied by a sound like wind, for three consecutive nights. Initially, everyone mistakenly thought it was a fire and went out to rescue, but could not find anything. Unexpectedly, on the sixth night, a similar firelight appeared in the southwest corner of Shanghai. Therefore, its strangeness is recorded for those who study things to investigate and verify.
